<p><b>Lev Davidovich Bronstein</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[a]</a></sup> (7 November [<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 26 October] 1879 – 21 August 1940), better known as <b>Leon Trotsky</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[b]</a></sup> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[1]</a></sup> was a Russian revolutionary, political theorist and politician. Ideologically a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">communist</a>, he developed a variant of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Trotskyism" title="Trotskyism">Trotskyism</a>.
</p><p>Trotsky joined the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolshevik Party</a> a few weeks before the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> and became one of the leaders of the party. Once in government, Trotsky initially held the post of the Commissar for Foreign Affairs and was involved in the Brest-Litovsk negotiations with Germany as Russia pulled out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_War_One" title="World War One">World War One</a>. Trotsky became more prominent from March 1918 to January 1925 as the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> in the post of Commissar for Military and Naval Affairs. Trotsky was a vital leading figure in the Red victory in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwain200686-104_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain200686-104-4">[2]</a></sup> He was one of the seven members of the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_CPSU_Central_Committee" title="Politburo of the CPSU Central Committee">Politburo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996185_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996185-5">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_Joseph_Stalin" title="Rise of Joseph Stalin">rise of Joseph Stalin</a>, Trotsky was removed from his positions and eventually expelled from the Soviet Union in February 1929. He spent the rest of his life in exile and was assassinated in 1940 in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> by <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Mercader" title="Ramón Mercader">Ramón Mercader</a>, a Soviet <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> agent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[c]</a></sup>
</p><p>Trotsky was openly critical of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeilharz1987Chapters_2_and_3_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeilharz1987Chapters_2_and_3-8">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeal2015_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeal2015-9">[6]</a></sup> He was written out of the history books under Stalin and was one of the few Soviet political personalities who was not <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_(Soviet)" title="Rehabilitation (Soviet)">rehabilitated</a> by the Soviet administration under <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> in the 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003bvi_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003bvi-10">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span id="Childhood_and_family_.281879.E2.80.931895.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood_and_family_(1879–1895)">Childhood and family (1879–1895)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Childhood and family (1879–1895)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="636" data-file-width="366" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg/170px-Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg/255px-Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg/340px-Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leo_Trotzki_1888.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>8-year-old Lev Bronstein, 1888</div></div></div>
<p>Leon Trotsky was born Lev Davidovich Bronstein to David Leontyevich Bronstein (1847-1922) and Anna Lvovna (née Zhivotovskaya, 1850-1910) on 7 November 1879, the fifth child of a Ukrainian-Jewish family of wealthy farmers in Yanovka or Yanivka, in the <a href="/wiki/Kherson_Governorate" title="Kherson Governorate">Kherson governorate</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Bereslavka,_Ukraine" title="Bereslavka, Ukraine">Bereslavka</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>), a small village 24 kilometres (15 mi) from the nearest post office. His father, David Leontyevich, had lived in Poltava, and later moved to <a href="/wiki/Bereslavka,_Ukraine" title="Bereslavka, Ukraine">Bereslavka</a>, as it had a large Jewish community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7-12">[9]</a></sup> The language spoken at home was a mixture of Russian and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> (known as <a href="/wiki/Surzhyk" title="Surzhyk">Surzhyk</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010145_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010145-13">[10]</a></sup> Trotsky's younger sister, <a href="/wiki/Olga_Kameneva" title="Olga Kameneva">Olga</a>, who also grew up to be a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> and a Soviet politician, married the prominent Bolshevik <a href="/wiki/Lev_Kamenev" title="Lev Kamenev">Lev Kamenev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParrish199669_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParrish199669-14">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some authors, notably <a href="/wiki/Robert_Service_(historian)" title="Robert Service (historian)">Robert Service</a>, have claimed that Trotsky's childhood first name was the <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a> <i>Leiba</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService201011_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService201011-15">[12]</a></sup> The American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trotskyist" title="Trotskyist">Trotskyist</a> <a href="/wiki/David_North_(socialist)" title="David North (socialist)">David North</a> said that this was an assumption based on Trotsky's Jewish birth, but, contrary to Service's claims, there is no documentary evidence to support his using a Yiddish name, when that language was not spoken by his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010144-46_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010144-46-16">[13]</a></sup> Both North and political historian <a href="/wiki/Walter_Laqueur" title="Walter Laqueur">Walter Laqueur</a> wrote that Trotsky's childhood name was <i>Lyova</i>, a standard Russian diminutive of the name <i>Lev.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaqueur199059-60_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaqueur199059-60-17">[14]</a></sup> North has compared the speculation on Trotsky's given name to the undue emphasis given to his having a Jewish surname.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010144-146_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010144-146-18">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaqueur199059-60_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaqueur199059-60-17">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>When Trotsky was eight,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> his father sent him to <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> to be educated. He was enrolled in a German-language school, which became Russified during his years in Odessa as a result of the Imperial government's policy of <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lindemann2000_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lindemann2000-20">[17]</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Deutscher" title="Isaac Deutscher">Isaac Deutscher</a> notes in his biography of Trotsky, Odessa was then a bustling cosmopolitan port city, very unlike the typical Russian city of the time. This environment contributed to the development of the young man's international outlook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003aChapter_1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003aChapter_1-21">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Trotsky spoke French, English, and German to a good standard, he said in his autobiography <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Life_(Leon_Trotsky_autobiography)" title="My Life (Leon Trotsky autobiography)">My Life</a></i> that he was never perfectly fluent in any language but Russian and Ukrainian.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Page from his autobiography required (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Molinier" title="Raymond Molinier">Raymond Molinier</a> wrote that Trotsky spoke French fluently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Early_political_activities_and_life_.281896.E2.80.931917.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_political_activities_and_life_(1896–1917)">Early political activities and life (1896–1917)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early political activities and life (1896–1917)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Revolutionary_activity_and_imprisonment_.281896.E2.80.931898.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolutionary_activity_and_imprisonment_(1896–1898)">Revolutionary activity and imprisonment (1896–1898)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Revolutionary activity and imprisonment (1896–1898)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LeonTrotsky1897.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="429" decoding="async" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/LeonTrotsky1897.jpg/200px-LeonTrotsky1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/LeonTrotsky1897.jpg/300px-LeonTrotsky1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/LeonTrotsky1897.jpg/400px-LeonTrotsky1897.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LeonTrotsky1897.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lev Davidovich Bronstein, 1897</div></div></div>
<p>Trotsky became involved in revolutionary activities in 1896 after moving to the harbor town of Nikolayev (now <a href="/wiki/Mykolaiv" title="Mykolaiv">Mykolaiv</a>) on the Ukrainian coast of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a36_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a36-23">[20]</a></sup> At first a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narodnik" title="Narodnik">narodnik</a></i> (revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_socialism" title="Agrarian socialism">agrarian socialist</a> <a href="/wiki/Populism" title="Populism">populist</a>), he initially opposed <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> but was won over to Marxism later that year by his future first wife, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandra_Sokolovskaya" title="Aleksandra Sokolovskaya">Aleksandra Sokolovskaya</a>. Instead of pursuing a mathematics degree, Trotsky helped organize the South Russian Workers' Union in Nikolayev in early 1897. Using the name "Lvov",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-24">[21]</a></sup> he wrote and printed leaflets and proclamations, distributed revolutionary pamphlets, and popularized socialist ideas among industrial workers and revolutionary students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenton200422-24_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenton200422-24-25">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 1898, more than 200 members of the union, including Trotsky, were arrested. He was held for the next two years in prison waiting trial, first in Nikolayev, then <a href="/wiki/Kherson" title="Kherson">Kherson</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, and finally in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> In the Moscow prison, he came into contact with other revolutionaries, heard about Lenin and read Lenin's book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Development_of_Capitalism_in_Russia" title="The Development of Capitalism in Russia">The Development of Capitalism in Russia</a></i>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a40_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a40-27">[24]</a></sup> Two months into his imprisonment, on 1–3 March 1898, the first Congress of the newly formed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Social_Democratic_Labor_Party" title="Russian Social Democratic Labor Party">Russian Social Democratic Labor Party</a> (RSDLP) was held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchapiro1970645_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchapiro1970645-28">[25]</a></sup> From then on Trotsky identified as a member of the party.
</p>
<h3><span id="First_marriage_and_Siberian_exile_.281899.E2.80.931902.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_marriage_and_Siberian_exile_(1899–1902)">First marriage and Siberian exile (1899–1902)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First marriage and Siberian exile (1899–1902)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_exile_of_Trotsky" title="First exile of Trotsky">First exile of Trotsky</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="406" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg/200px-Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg/300px-Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg/400px-Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leo_Trotzki_1897.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky's first wife Aleksandra Sokolovskaya with her brother (sitting on the left) and Trotsky (sitting on the right) in 1897</div></div></div>
<p>While in the prison in Moscow, in the summer of 1899, Trotsky married <a href="/wiki/Aleksandra_Sokolovskaya" title="Aleksandra Sokolovskaya">Aleksandra Sokolovskaya</a> (1872–1938), a fellow Marxist.  The wedding ceremony was performed by a Jewish chaplain. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a42_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a42-29">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1900, he was sentenced to four years in exile in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. Because of their marriage, Trotsky and his wife were allowed to be exiled to the same location in Siberia. They were exiled to <a href="/wiki/Ust-Kut" title="Ust-Kut">Ust-Kut</a> and the Verkholensk in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baikal_Lake" title="Baikal Lake">Baikal Lake</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>.  They had two daughters, <a href="/wiki/Zinaida_Volkova" title="Zinaida Volkova">Zinaida</a> (1901 – 5 January 1933) and Nina (1902 – 9 June 1928), both born in Siberia.
</p><p>In Siberia, Trotsky studied philosophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarth197822_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarth197822-30">[27]</a></sup> He became aware of the differences within the party, which had been decimated by arrests in 1898 and 1899. Some social democrats known as "economists" argued that the party should focus on helping industrial workers improve their lot in life and were not so worried about changing the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchapiro197031-32_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchapiro197031-32-31">[28]</a></sup> They believed that societal reforms would grow out of the worker's struggle for higher pay and better working conditions. Others argued that overthrowing the monarchy was more important and that a well-organized and disciplined revolutionary party was essential. The latter position was expressed by the London-based newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Iskra" title="Iskra">Iskra</a>,</i> (<i>The Spark,</i>) which was founded in 1900. Trotsky quickly sided with the <i>Iskra</i> position and began writing for the paper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a67_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a67-32">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the summer of 1902, at the urging of his wife Aleksandra, Trotsky escaped from Siberia hidden in a load of hay on a wagon. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a55_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a55-33">[30]</a></sup> Aleksandra later escaped from Siberia with their daughters. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarth197822_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarth197822-30">[27]</a></sup> Both daughters married, and Zinaida had children, but the daughters died before their parents. Nina Nevelson died from <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> in 1928, cared for in her last months by her older sister. Zinaida Volkova followed her father into exile in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, taking her son by her second marriage but leaving behind a daughter in Russia. Suffering also from tuberculosis and <a href="/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">depression</a>, Zinaida committed suicide in 1933. Aleksandra disappeared in 1935 during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purges</a> in the Soviet Union under Stalin and was murdered by Stalinist forces three years later.
</p>
<h3><span id="First_emigration_and_second_marriage_.281902.E2.80.931903.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_emigration_and_second_marriage_(1902–1903)">First emigration and second marriage (1902–1903)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First emigration and second marriage (1902–1903)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:transparent;border-top:1px solid #aaa;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Category:Marxists" title="Category:Marxists">People</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center"><div class="hlist">

<div class="CategoryTreeTag" data-ct-mode="20" data-ct-options='{"mode":20,"hideprefix":20,"showcount":false,"namespaces":false,"notranslations":false}'><div class="CategoryTreeSection"><div class="CategoryTreeItem"><span class="CategoryTreeBullet"><span class="CategoryTreeToggle" data-ct-state="collapsed" data-ct-title="Karl_Marx">►</span> </span> <a href="/wiki/Category:Karl_Marx" title="Category:Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a></div><div class="CategoryTreeChildren" style="display:none"></div></div></div>
</div></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="plainlist" style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;line-height:1.6em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Marxism" title="Outline of Marxism">Outline</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg"><img alt="Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg/16px-Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg/24px-Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg/32px-Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Communism" title="Portal:Communism">Communism portal</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Socrates.png"><img alt="Socrates.png" class="noviewer" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="326" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/10px-Socrates.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/15px-Socrates.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/21px-Socrates.png 2x" width="10"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Philosophy" title="Portal:Philosophy">Philosophy portal</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red_flag_II.svg"><img alt="Red flag II.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="466" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Red_flag_II.svg/16px-Red_flag_II.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Red_flag_II.svg/24px-Red_flag_II.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Red_flag_II.svg/32px-Red_flag_II.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Socialism" title="Portal:Socialism">Socialism portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Marxism_sidebar" title="Template:Marxism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Marxism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Marxism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Marxism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Until this point in his life, Trotsky had used his birth name: Lev (Leon) Bronstein. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a7_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a7-34">[31]</a></sup> He changed his surname to "Trotsky"—the name he would use for the rest of his life. It is said he adopted the name of a jailer of the Odessa prison in which he had earlier been held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> This became his primary revolutionary pseudonym. After his escape from Siberia, Trotsky moved to London, joining <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Plekhanov" title="Georgi Plekhanov">Georgi Plekhanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Martov" title="Julius Martov">Julius Martov</a> and other editors of <i>Iskra</i>. Under the pen name <i>Pero</i> ("feather" or "pen"), Trotsky soon became one of the paper's leading writers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7-12">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unknown to Trotsky, the six editors of <i>Iskra</i> were evenly split between the "old guard" led by <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Plekhanov" title="Georgi Plekhanov">Plekhanov</a> and the "new guard" led by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julius_Martov" title="Julius Martov">Martov</a>. Plekhanov's supporters were older (in their 40s and 50s), and had spent the previous 20 years together in exile in Europe. Members of the new guard were in their early 30s and had only recently emigrated from Russia. Lenin, who was trying to establish a permanent majority against Plekhanov within <i>Iskra,</i> expected Trotsky, then 23, to side with the new guard. In March 1903 Lenin wrote:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r960796168">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I suggest to all the members of the editorial board that they co-opt 'Pero' as a member of the board on the same basis as other members. [...] We very much need a seventh member, both as a convenience in voting (six being an even number) and as an addition to our forces. 'Pero' has been contributing to every issue for several months now; he works, in general, most energetically for the Iskra; he gives lectures (in which he has been very successful). In the section of articles and notes on the events of the day, he will not only be very useful, but absolutely necessary. Unquestionably a man of rare abilities, he has conviction and energy, and he will go much farther.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Because of Plekhanov's opposition, Trotsky did not become a full member of the board. But from then on, he participated in its meetings in an advisory capacity, which earned him Plekhanov's enmity.
</p><p>In late 1902, Trotsky met <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Sedova" title="Natalia Sedova">Natalia Sedova</a> (1882 – 1962), who soon became his companion. They married in 1903, and she was with him until his death. They had two children together, <a href="/wiki/Lev_Sedov" title="Lev Sedov">Lev Sedov</a> (24 February 1906 – 16 February 1938) and <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Sedov" title="Sergei Sedov">Sergei Sedov</a> (21 March 1908 – 29 October 1937), both of whom would predecease their parents. Regarding his sons' surnames, Trotsky later explained that after the 1917 revolution:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In order not to oblige my sons to change their name, I, for "citizenship" requirements, took on the name of my wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Trotsky never used the name "Sedov" either privately or publicly. Natalia Sedova sometimes signed her name "Sedova-Trotskaya".
</p>
<h3><span id="Split_with_Lenin_.281903.E2.80.931904.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Split_with_Lenin_(1903–1904)">Split with Lenin (1903–1904)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Split with Lenin (1903–1904)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_(%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="928" data-file-width="827" decoding="async" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902%29.jpg/220px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902%29.jpg/330px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902%29.jpg/440px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%81%D1%8B%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B8_(%D0%BE%D0%BA._1902).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky in 1902</div></div></div>
<p>In the meantime, after a period of secret police repression and internal confusion that followed the <a href="/wiki/1st_Congress_of_the_Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party" title="1st Congress of the Russian Social Democratic Labour Party">First Congress of the Russian Social Democratic Labour Party</a> in 1898, <i>Iskra</i> succeeded in convening the party's <a href="/wiki/2nd_Congress_of_the_Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party" title="2nd Congress of the Russian Social Democratic Labour Party">Second Congress</a> in London in August 1903. Trotsky and other <i>Iskra</i> editors attended. The first congress went as planned, with <i>Iskra</i> supporters handily defeating the few "economist" delegates. Then the congress discussed the position of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Jewish_Labour_Bund_in_Lithuania,_Poland_and_Russia" title="General Jewish Labour Bund in Lithuania, Poland and Russia">Jewish Bund</a>, which had co-founded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RSDLP" title="RSDLP">RSDLP</a> in 1898 but wanted to remain autonomous within the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-38">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly after that, the pro-Iskra delegates split into two factions. Lenin and his supporters, the Bolsheviks, argued for a smaller but highly organized party, while Martov and his supporters, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Menshevik" title="Menshevik">Mensheviks</a>, argued for a more massive and less disciplined party. In a surprise development, Trotsky and most of the Iskra editors supported Martov and the Mensheviks, while Plekhanov supported Lenin and the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a>. During 1903 and 1904, many members changed sides in the factions. Plekhanov soon parted ways with the Bolsheviks. Trotsky left the Mensheviks in September 1904 over their insistence on an alliance with Russian liberals and their opposition to a reconciliation with Lenin and the Bolsheviks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1904 until 1917, Trotsky described himself as a "non-factional social democrat". He worked between 1904 and 1917, trying to reconcile different groups within the party, which resulted in many clashes with Lenin and other prominent party members. Trotsky later maintained that he had been wrong in opposing Lenin on the issue of the party. During these years, Trotsky began developing his theory of <a href="/wiki/Permanent_revolution" title="Permanent revolution">permanent revolution</a> and developed a close working relationship with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Parvus" title="Alexander Parvus">Alexander Parvus</a> in 1904–07.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>During their split, Lenin referred to Trotsky as a "<a href="/wiki/Judas_Iscariot" title="Judas Iscariot">Judas</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> a "scoundrel"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> and a "swine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1905_revolution_and_trial_.281905.E2.80.931906.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1905_revolution_and_trial_(1905–1906)">1905 revolution and trial (1905–1906)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1905 revolution and trial (1905–1906)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The unrest and agitation against the Russian government came to a head in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> on 3 January 1905 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_Calendar" title="Julian Calendar">Julian Calendar</a>), when a strike broke out at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Putilov_Works" title="Putilov Works">Putilov Works</a> in the city. This single strike grew into a general strike, and by 7 January 1905, there were 140,000 strikers in Saint Petersburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>On Sunday, 9 January 1905, Father <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgi_Gapon" title="Georgi Gapon">Georgi Gapon</a> led a peaceful procession of citizens through the streets to the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">Winter Palace</a> to beseech the Tsar for food and relief from the oppressive government. The Palace Guard fired on the peaceful demonstration, resulting in the deaths of some 1,000 demonstrators. Sunday, 9 January 1905, became known as <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Sunday_(1905)" title="Bloody Sunday (1905)">Bloody Sunday</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7-12">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trotskymugshots.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="724" data-file-width="1454" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Trotskymugshots.jpg/330px-Trotskymugshots.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Trotskymugshots.jpg/495px-Trotskymugshots.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Trotskymugshots.jpg/660px-Trotskymugshots.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trotskymugshots.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Police mugshots of Trotsky in 1905 after Soviet members were arrested during a meeting in the Free Economic Society building</div></div></div>
<p>Following the events of Bloody Sunday, Trotsky secretly returned to Russia in February 1905, by way of <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a117_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a117-45">[42]</a></sup> At first he wrote leaflets for an underground printing press in Kyiv, but soon moved to the capital, Saint Petersburg. There he worked with both Bolsheviks, such as Central Committee member <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Krasin" title="Leonid Krasin">Leonid Krasin</a>, and the local Menshevik committee, which he pushed in a more radical direction. The latter, however, were betrayed by a secret police agent in May, and Trotsky had to flee to rural <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Finland" title="Grand Duchy of Finland">Finland</a>. There he worked on fleshing out his theory of permanent revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 September 1905, the typesetters at the <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sytin" title="Ivan Sytin">Ivan Sytin</a>'s printing house in Moscow went out on strike for shorter hours and higher pay. By the evening of 24 September, the workers at 50 other printing shops in Moscow were also on strike. On 2 October 1905, the typesetters in printing shops in Saint Petersburg decided to strike in support of the Moscow strikers. On 7 October 1905, the railway workers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow-Kazan_Railway" title="Moscow-Kazan Railway">Moscow–Kazan Railway</a> went out on strike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> Amid the resulting confusion, Trotsky returned from Finland to Saint Petersburg on 15 October 1905. On that day, Trotsky spoke before the Saint Petersburg Soviet Council of Workers Deputies, which was meeting at the Technological Institute in the city. Also attending were some 200,000 people crowded outside to hear the speeches—about half of all workers in Saint Petersburg. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a126_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a126-48">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1918" data-file-width="1223" decoding="async" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png/220px-TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png/330px-TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png/440px-TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TrotskiEnLaFortalezaDePedroYPabloEn1906.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky in prison, awaiting trial, 1905</div></div></div>
<p>After his return, Trotsky and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parvus" title="Parvus">Parvus</a> took over the newspaper <i>Russian Gazette,</i> increasing its circulation to 500,000. Trotsky also co-founded, together with Parvus and <a href="/wiki/Julius_Martov" title="Julius Martov">Julius Martov</a> and other Mensheviks, “Nachalo" ("The Beginning"), which also proved to be a very successful newspaper in the revolutionary atmosphere of Saint Petersburg in 1905. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a138–39_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a138–39-49">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Just before Trotsky's return, the Mensheviks had independently come up with the same idea that Trotsky had: an elected non-party revolutionary organization representing the capital's workers, the first <a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">Soviet</a> ("Council") of Workers. By the time of Trotsky's arrival, the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Soviet" title="Saint Petersburg Soviet">Saint Petersburg Soviet</a> was already functioning headed by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Khrustalyev-Nosar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Khrustalyev-Nosar (page does not exist)">Khrustalyev-Nosar</a> (Georgy Nosar, alias Pyotr Khrustalyov). Khrustalyev-Nosar had been a compromise figure when elected as the head of the Saint Petersburg Soviet. Khrustalev-Nosar was a lawyer that stood above the political factions contained in the Soviet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a131_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a131-50">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>
However, since his election, he proved to be very popular with the workers in spite of the Bolsheviks' original opposition to him. Khrustalev-Nosar became famous in his position as spokesman for the Saint Petersburg Soviet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup>  Indeed, to the outside world, Khrustalev-Nosar was the embodiment of the Saint Petersburg Soviet. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a131_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a131-50">[47]</a></sup> Trotsky joined the Soviet under the name "Yanovsky" (after the village he was born in, Yanovka) and was elected vice-chairman. He did much of the actual work at the Soviet and, after Khrustalev-Nosar's arrest on 26 November 1905, was elected its chairman. On 2 December, the Soviet issued a proclamation which included the following statement about the Tsarist government and its foreign debts:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The autocracy never enjoyed the confidence of the people and was never granted any authority by the people. We have therefore decided not to allow the repayment of such loans as have been made by the Tsarist government when openly engaged in a war with the entire people.</p></blockquote>
<p>The following day, the Soviet was surrounded by troops loyal to the government and the deputies were arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> Trotsky and other Soviet leaders were tried in 1906 on charges of supporting an armed rebellion. On 4 October 1906 he was convicted and sentenced to internal exile to Siberia.
</p>
<h3><span id="Second_emigration_.281907.E2.80.931914.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_emigration_(1907–1914)">Second emigration (1907–1914)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second emigration (1907–1914)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="536" data-file-width="647" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg/220px-ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg/330px-ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg/440px-ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ParvusTrotskiDeich.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Parvus" title="Alexander Parvus">Alexander Parvus</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Leo_Deutsch" title="Leo Deutsch">Leo Deutsch</a> (right) in Saint Peter and Paul Fortress prison at Saint Petersburg in 1906</div></div></div>
<p>While en route to exile in <a href="/wiki/Salekhard" title="Salekhard">Obdorsk</a>, Siberia, in January 1907, Trotsky escaped at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beryozovo" title="Beryozovo">Berezov</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> and once again made his way to London. He attended the <a href="/wiki/5th_Congress_of_the_Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party" title="5th Congress of the Russian Social Democratic Labour Party">5th Congress of the RSDLP</a>. In October, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, Austria-Hungary. For the next seven years, he often took part in the activities of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Austrian Social Democratic Party">Austrian Social Democratic Party</a> and, occasionally, of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Social_Democratic_Party" title="German Social Democratic Party">German Social Democratic Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-38">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Vienna, Trotsky became close to <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Joffe" title="Adolph Joffe">Adolph Joffe</a>, his friend for the next 20 years, who introduced him to <a href="/wiki/Psychoanalysis" title="Psychoanalysis">psychoanalysis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%87%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%E2%80%9E%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B0%E2%80%9C_%D0%B2_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5_(%D0%BE%D0%BA._1910).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="314" decoding="async" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%87%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%E2%80%9E%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B0%E2%80%9C_%D0%B2_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1910%29.jpg/220px-%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%87%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%E2%80%9E%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B0%E2%80%9C_%D0%B2_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1910%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%87%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%E2%80%9E%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B0%E2%80%9C_%D0%B2_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5_%28%D0%BE%D0%BA._1910%29.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%87%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%E2%80%9E%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B0%E2%80%9C_%D0%B2_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5_(%D0%BE%D0%BA._1910).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky reading the <i>Pravda</i> in Vienna, circa 1910</div></div></div>
<p>In October 1908 he was asked to join the editorial staff of <i><a href="/wiki/Pravda" title="Pravda">Pravda</a></i> ("Truth"), a bi-weekly, Russian-language social democratic paper for Russian workers, which he co-edited with <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Joffe" title="Adolph Joffe">Adolph Joffe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matvey_Skobelev" title="Matvey Skobelev">Matvey Skobelev</a>. It was smuggled into Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a191_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a191-56">[53]</a></sup> The paper appeared very irregularly; only five issues were published in its first year. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a191_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a191-56">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Avoiding factional politics, the paper proved popular with Russian industrial workers. Both the Bolsheviks and the Mensheviks split multiple times after the failure of the 1905–1907 revolution. Money was very scarce for the publication of “<a href="/wiki/Pravda" title="Pravda">Pravda</a>"<i>.</i> Trotsky approached the Russian Central Committee to seek financial backing for the newspaper throughout 1909. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a192_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a192-57">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>A majority of Bolsheviks controlled the Central Committee in 1910. Lenin agreed to the financing of “Pravda" but required a Bolshevik to be appointed as co-editor of the paper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a192_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a192-57">[54]</a></sup> When various Bolshevik and Menshevik factions tried to re-unite at the January 1910 RSDLP Central Committee meeting in Paris over Lenin's objections,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> Trotsky's <i>Pravda</i> was made a party-financed 'central organ'. <a href="/wiki/Lev_Kamenev" title="Lev Kamenev">Lev Kamenev</a>, Trotsky's brother-in-law, was added to the editorial board from the Bolsheviks, but the unification attempts failed in August 1910. Kamenev resigned from the board amid mutual recriminations. Trotsky continued publishing <a href="/wiki/Pravda" title="Pravda">Pravda</a> for another two years until it finally folded in April 1912.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003aChapter_1_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003aChapter_1-21">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bolsheviks started a new workers-oriented newspaper in Saint Petersburg on 22 April 1912 and also called it <i>Pravda</i>. Trotsky was so upset by what he saw as a usurpation of his newspaper's name that in April 1913, he wrote a letter to <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Chkheidze" title="Nikolay Chkheidze">Nikolay Chkheidze</a>, a Menshevik leader, bitterly denouncing Lenin and the Bolsheviks. Though he quickly got over the disagreement, the message was intercepted by the <a href="/wiki/Okhrana" title="Okhrana">Russian police</a>, and a copy was put into their archives. Shortly after Lenin's death in 1924, the letter was found and publicized by Trotsky's opponents within the Communist Party to portray him as Lenin's enemy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a-6-7-12">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1910s was a period of heightened tension within the RSDLP, leading to numerous frictions between Trotsky, the Bolsheviks and the Mensheviks. The most serious disagreement that Trotsky and the Mensheviks had with Lenin at the time was over the issue of "expropriations",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> i.e., armed robbery of banks and other companies by Bolshevik groups to procure money for the Party. These actions had been banned by the 5th Congress, but were continued by the Bolsheviks.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="386" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg/220px-Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg/330px-Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg/440px-Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trotsky_in_Vienna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky in Vienna</div></div></div>
<p>In January 1912, the majority of the Bolshevik faction, led by Lenin, as well as a few defecting Mensheviks, held a conference in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and decided to break away from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party" title="Russian Social Democratic Labour Party">Russian Social Democratic Labour Party</a>, and formed a new party, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Russian Social Democratic Labour Party (Bolsheviks)</a>. In response, Trotsky organized a "unification" conference of social democratic factions in Vienna in August 1912 (a.k.a. "The August Bloc") and tried to re-unite the Bolsheviks and Mensheviks into one party. The attempt was generally unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-:3-38">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, Trotsky continuously published articles in radical Russian and Ukrainian newspapers, such as <i>Kievskaya Mysl,</i> under a variety of pseudonyms, often using "Antid Oto”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService201062_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService201062-60">[57]</a></sup> In September 1912, <i>Kievskaya Mysl</i> sent him to the Balkans as its war correspondent, where he covered the two <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> for the next year. While there, Trotsky chronicled the ethnic cleansing carried out by the Serbian army against the Albanian civilian population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> He became a close friend of <a href="/wiki/Christian_Rakovsky" title="Christian Rakovsky">Christian Rakovsky</a>, later a leading Soviet politician and Trotsky's ally in the Soviet Communist Party. On 3 August 1914, at the outbreak of World War I, in which <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> fought against the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, Trotsky was forced to flee Vienna for neutral Switzerland to avoid arrest as a Russian <a href="/wiki/%C3%89migr%C3%A9" title="Émigré">émigré</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-24">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="World_War_I_.281914.E2.80.931917.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I_(1914–1917)">World War I (1914–1917)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: World War I (1914–1917)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The outbreak of World War I caused a sudden realignment within the RSDLP and other European social democratic parties over the issues of war, revolution, pacifism and internationalism. Within the RSDLP, Lenin, Trotsky and Martov advocated various internationalist anti-war positions, while Plekhanov and other social democrats (both Bolsheviks and Mensheviks) supported the Russian government to some extent. In <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, Trotsky briefly worked within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Socialist_Party" title="Swiss Socialist Party">Swiss Socialist Party</a>, prompting it to adopt an internationalist resolution. He wrote a book opposing the war, <i>The War and the International,</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> and the pro-war position taken by the European social democratic parties, primarily the German party.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trotskynina1915.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="369" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Trotskynina1915.jpg/170px-Trotskynina1915.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Trotskynina1915.jpg/255px-Trotskynina1915.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Trotskynina1915.jpg/340px-Trotskynina1915.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trotskynina1915.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leon Trotsky with his daughter Nina in 1915</div></div></div>
<p>As a war correspondent for the <i>Kievskaya Mysl</i>, Trotsky moved to France on 19 November 1914. In January 1915 in Paris, he began editing (at first with Martov, who soon resigned as the paper moved to the left) <i><a href="/wiki/Nashe_Slovo" title="Nashe Slovo">Nashe Slovo</a></i> ("Our Word"), an internationalist socialist newspaper. He adopted the slogan of "peace without indemnities or annexations, peace without conquerors or conquered." Lenin advocated Russia's defeat in the war and demanded a complete break with the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>Trotsky attended the <a href="/wiki/Zimmerwald_Conference" title="Zimmerwald Conference">Zimmerwald Conference</a> of anti-war socialists in September 1915 and advocated a middle course between those who, like Martov, would stay within the Second International at any cost and those who, like Lenin, would break with the Second International and form a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_International" title="Third International">Third International</a>. The conference adopted the middle line proposed by Trotsky. At first opposed, in the end Lenin voted for Trotsky's resolution to avoid a split among anti-war socialists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 March 1916<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, Trotsky was deported from France to Spain for his anti-war activities. Spanish authorities did not want him and deported him to the United States on 25 December 1916. He arrived in New York City on 13 January 1917. He stayed for nearly three months at 1522 Vyse Avenue in <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">The Bronx</a>. In New York he wrote articles for the local <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a> socialist newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/Novy_Mir_(1916_magazine)" title="Novy Mir (1916 magazine)">Novy Mir</a>,</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a>-language daily, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Daily_Forward" title="The Jewish Daily Forward"><i>Der Forverts</i> (<i>The Jewish Daily Forward</i>)</a>, in translation. He also made speeches to Russian émigrés.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-65">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Trotsky was living in New York City when the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> of 1917 overthrew <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Tsar Nicholas II</a>. He left New York on 27 March 1917, but his ship, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Kristianiafjord" title="SS Kristianiafjord">SS Kristianiafjord</a>,</i> was intercepted by <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">British naval</a> officials in Canada at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a>. He was detained for a month at <a href="/wiki/Amherst_Internment_Camp" title="Amherst Internment Camp">Amherst Internment Camp</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>. While imprisoned in the camp, Trotsky established an increasing friendship with the workers and sailors amongst his fellow inmates, describing his month at the camp as "one continual mass meeting".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ns1758.ca_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-ns1758.ca-66">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Trotsky's speeches and agitation incurred the wrath of German officer inmates who complained to the British camp commander, Colonel Morris, about Trotsky's "anti-patriotic" attitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ns1758.ca_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-ns1758.ca-66">[63]</a></sup> Morris then forbade Trotsky to make any more public speeches, leading to 530 prisoners protesting and signing a petition against Morris' order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ns1758.ca_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-ns1758.ca-66">[63]</a></sup> Back in Russia, after initial hesitation and facing pressure from the workers' and peasants' <a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">soviets</a>, the Russian foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Milyukov" title="Pavel Milyukov">Pavel Milyukov</a> was compelled to demand the release of Trotsky as a Russian citizen, and the British government freed him on 29 April 1917.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ns1758.ca_66-3"><a href="#cite_note-ns1758.ca-66">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="749" data-file-width="516" decoding="async" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg/220px-Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg/330px-Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg/440px-Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leo_Trotzki_1917.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trotsky arriving in Petrograd by train in May 1917.</div></div></div>
<p>He reached Russia on 17 May 1917. After his return, Trotsky substantially agreed with the Bolshevik position, but did not join them right away. Russian social democrats were split into at least six groups, and the Bolsheviks were waiting for the next party Congress to determine which factions to merge with. Trotsky temporarily joined the <a href="/wiki/Mezhraiontsy" title="Mezhraiontsy">Mezhraiontsy</a>, a regional social democratic organization in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, and became one of its leaders. At the First <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Soviets" title="Congress of Soviets">Congress of Soviets</a> in June, he was elected a member of the first <a href="/wiki/All-Russian_Central_Executive_Committee" title="All-Russian Central Executive Committee">All-Russian Central Executive Committee</a> ("VTsIK") from the Mezhraiontsy faction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>After an unsuccessful pro-Bolshevik uprising in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Petrograd</a>, Trotsky was arrested on 7 August 1917. He was released 40 days later in the aftermath of the failed counter-revolutionary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kornilov_Affair" title="Kornilov Affair">uprising by Lavr Kornilov</a>. After the Bolsheviks gained a majority in the <a href="/wiki/Petrograd_Soviet" title="Petrograd Soviet">Petrograd Soviet</a>, Trotsky was elected chairman on 25 September [<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 8 October] 1917.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wade_p._xxi_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wade_p._xxi-68">[65]</a></sup> He sided with Lenin against <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Zinoviev" title="Grigory Zinoviev">Grigory Zinoviev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lev_Kamenev" title="Lev Kamenev">Lev Kamenev</a> when the Bolshevik Central Committee discussed staging an armed uprising, and he led the efforts to overthrow the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government,_1917" title="Russian Provisional Government, 1917">Provisional Government</a> headed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Kerensky" title="Aleksandr Kerensky">Aleksandr Kerensky</a>.
</p><p>The following summary of Trotsky's role in 1917 was written by Stalin in <i>Pravda</i>, 6 November 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI26_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-NI26-69">[66]</a></sup> Although this passage was quoted in Stalin's book <i>The October Revolution</i> (1934),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI26_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-NI26-69">[66]</a></sup> it was expunged from Stalin's <i>Works</i> (1949).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>All practical work in connection with the organization of the uprising was done under the immediate direction of Comrade Trotsky, the President of the Petrograd Soviet. It can be stated with certainty that the Party is indebted primarily and principally to Comrade Trotsky for the rapid going over of the garrison to the side of the Soviet and the efficient manner in which the work of the <a href="/wiki/Military_Revolutionary_Committee" title="Military Revolutionary Committee">Military Revolutionary Committee</a> was organized.</p></blockquote>
<p>After the success of the uprising on 7–8 November 1917, Trotsky led the efforts to repel a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerensky-Krasnov_uprising" title="Kerensky-Krasnov uprising">counter-attack</a> by <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a> under General <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Krasnov" title="Pyotr Krasnov">Pyotr Krasnov</a> and other troops still loyal to the overthrown Provisional Government at <a href="/wiki/Gatchina" title="Gatchina">Gatchina</a>. Allied with Lenin, he defeated attempts by other Bolshevik Central Committee members (Zinoviev, Kamenev, Rykov, etc.) to share power with other socialist parties. By the end of 1917, Trotsky was unquestionably the second man in the Bolshevik Party after Lenin. He overshadowed the ambitious Zinoviev, who had been Lenin's top lieutenant over the previous decade, but whose star appeared to be fading. This reversal of position contributed to continuing competition and enmity between the two men, which lasted until 1926 and did much to destroy them both.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Revolution_and_aftermath">Russian Revolution and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Russian Revolution and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Commissar_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Brest-Litovsk_.281917.E2.80.931918.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Commissar_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Brest-Litovsk_(1917–1918)">Commissar for Foreign Affairs and Brest-Litovsk (1917–1918)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Commissar for Foreign Affairs and Brest-Litovsk (1917–1918)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="589" data-file-width="635" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg/220px-Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg/330px-Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg/440px-Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_Lev_Kamenev_Brest-Litovsk_negotiations.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leon Trotsky and <a href="/wiki/Lev_Kamenev" title="Lev Kamenev">Lev Kamenev</a> at <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk">Brest-Litovsk negotiations</a> (c. 1917–1918)</div></div></div>
<p>After the Bolsheviks came to power, Trotsky became the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Soviet_Union)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Soviet Union)">People's Commissar for Foreign Affairs</a> and published the <a href="/wiki/Secret_treaty" title="Secret treaty">secret treaties</a> previously signed by the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> that detailed plans for post-war reallocation of colonies and redrawing state borders.
</p><p>Trotsky led the Soviet delegation during the peace negotiations in <a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest-Litovsk</a> from 22 December 1917 to 10 February 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> At that time the Soviet government was split on the issue. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_Communism" title="Left Communism">Left Communists</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin" title="Nikolai Bukharin">Nikolai Bukharin</a>, continued to believe that there could be no peace between a Soviet republic and a capitalist country and that only a revolutionary war leading to a pan-European Soviet republic would bring a durable peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leon_Trotsky_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leon_Trotsky-72">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>They cited the successes of the newly formed (15 January 1918) voluntary <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> against Polish forces of Gen. <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Dowbor-Mu%C5%9Bnicki" title="Józef Dowbor-Muśnicki">Józef Dowbor-Muśnicki</a> in Belarus, <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White</a> forces in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_River,_Russia" title="Don River, Russia">Don</a> region, and newly independent <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> forces as proof that the Red Army could repel German forces, especially if propaganda and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asymmetrical_warfare" title="Asymmetrical warfare">asymmetrical warfare</a> were used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leon_Trotsky_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leon_Trotsky-72">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>They were willing to hold talks with the Germans as a means of exposing German imperial ambitions (territorial gains, <a href="/wiki/War_reparations" title="War reparations">reparations</a>, etc.) in the hope of accelerating the hoped−for Soviet revolution in the West. Still, they were dead set against signing any peace treaty. In the case of a German ultimatum, they advocated proclaiming a revolutionary war against Germany to inspire Russian and European workers to fight for socialism. This opinion was shared by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_Socialist_Revolutionaries" title="Left Socialist Revolutionaries">Left Socialist Revolutionaries</a>, who were then the Bolsheviks' junior partners in a coalition government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lsrm_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-lsrm-73">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="916" data-file-width="589" decoding="async" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg/170px-Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg/255px-Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg/340px-Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk-en.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Territory lost under the Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</div></div></div><p>
Lenin, who had earlier hoped for a speedy Soviet revolution in Germany and other parts of Europe, quickly decided that the imperial government of Germany was still firmly in control and that, without a strong Russian military, an armed conflict with Germany would lead to a collapse of the Soviet government in Russia. He agreed with the Left Communists that ultimately a pan-European Soviet revolution would solve all problems, but until then the Bolsheviks had to stay in power. Lenin did not mind prolonging the negotiating process for maximum propaganda effect, but, from January 1918 on, advocated signing a separate peace treaty if faced with a German ultimatum. Trotsky's position was between these two Bolshevik factions. Like Lenin, he admitted that the old Russian military, inherited from the monarchy and the Provisional Government and in advanced stages of decomposition, was unable to fight:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>That we could no longer fight was perfectly clear to me and that the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Red_Guards_(Russia)" title="Red Guards (Russia)">Red Guard</a> and Red Army detachments were too small and poorly trained to resist the Germans.</p></blockquote><p>
But he agreed with the Left Communists that a separate peace treaty with an imperialist power would be a terrible morale and material blow to the Soviet government, negate all its military and political successes of 1917 and 1918, resurrect the notion that the Bolsheviks secretly allied with the German government, and cause an upsurge of internal resistance. He argued that any German ultimatum should be refused, and that this might well lead to an uprising in Germany, or at least inspire German soldiers to disobey their officers since any German offensive would be a naked grab for territories. Trotsky wrote in 1925:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We began peace negotiations in the hope of arousing the workmen's party of Germany and Austria-Hungary as well as of the Entente countries. For this reason we were obliged to delay the negotiations as long as possible to give the European workman time to understand the main fact of the Soviet revolution itself and particularly its peace policy. But there was the other question: Can the Germans still fight? Are they in a position to begin an attack on the revolution that will explain the cessation of the war? How can we find out the state of mind of the German soldiers, how to fathom it?</p></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="510" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg/220px-Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg/330px-Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg/440px-Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Protecci%C3%B3n_del_Palacio_Tauride_durante_el_Segundo_Congreso_Regional_de_los_Soviets.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constituent_Assembly" title="Russian Constituent Assembly">Constituent Assembly</a> on 6 January 1918. The <a href="/wiki/Tauride_Palace" title="Tauride Palace">Tauride Palace</a> is locked and guarded by Trotsky, <a href="/wiki/Yakov_Sverdlov" title="Yakov Sverdlov">Sverdlov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Zinoviev" title="Grigory Zinoviev">Zinoviev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lashevich" title="Mikhail Lashevich">Lashevich</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout January and February 1918, Lenin's position was supported by 7 members of the Bolshevik Central Committee and Bukharin's by 4. Trotsky had 4 votes (his own, <a href="/wiki/Felix_Dzerzhinsky" title="Felix Dzerzhinsky">Felix Dzerzhinsky</a>'s, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Krestinsky" title="Nikolai Krestinsky">Nikolai Krestinsky</a>'s and <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Joffe" title="Adolph Joffe">Adolph Joffe</a>'s) and, since he held the balance of power, he was able to pursue his policy in Brest-Litovsk. When he could no longer delay the negotiations, he withdrew from the talks on 10 February 1918, refusing to sign on Germany's harsh terms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>After a brief hiatus, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> notified the Soviet government that they would no longer observe the truce after 17 February. At this point Lenin again argued that the Soviet government had done all it could to explain its position to Western workers and that it was time to accept the terms. Trotsky refused to support Lenin since he was waiting to see whether German workers would rebel and whether German soldiers would refuse to follow orders.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Germany resumed <a href="/wiki/Operation_Faustschlag" title="Operation Faustschlag">military operations</a> on 18 February. Within a day, it became clear that the German army was capable of conducting offensive operations and that Red Army detachments, which were relatively small, poorly organized and poorly led, were no match for it.
