<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Russian and Ukrainian: Лев (Лейба) Давидович Бронштейн</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Russian: <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">Лев Давидович Троцкий</span>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[ˈlʲɛf ˈtrotskʲɪj]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ru-Leon_Trotsky.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/Ru-Leon_Trotsky.ogg" title="Ru-Leon Trotsky.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; Ukrainian: <span lang="uk">Лев Давидович Троцький</span>; also transliterated <i>Lyev</i>, <i>Trotski</i>, <i>Trotskij</i>, <i>Trockij</i> and <i>Trotzky</i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The murder weapon was a cut-down <a href="/wiki/Ice_axe" title="Ice axe">ice axe</a>, not an <a href="/wiki/Ice_pick" title="Ice pick">ice pick</a>. Many history and reference books have confused the two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConquest1992418_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConquest1992418-6">[4]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Yakov Sverdlov was the Central Committee's senior secretary responsible for personnel affairs from 1917 and until his death in March 1919. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Elena_Stasova" title="Elena Stasova">Elena Stasova</a>, and in November 1919 by Nikolai Krestinsky.

After Krestinsky's ouster in March 1921, Vyacheslav Molotov became the senior secretary, but he lacked Krestinsky's authority, since he was not a full Politburo member. Stalin took over the position as senior secretary, which was formalized at the XIth Party Congress in April 1922, with Molotov becoming second secretary.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is not clear why Kamenev, a mild-mannered man with few leadership ambitions and who was the brother-in-law of Trotsky, sided with Zinoviev and Stalin against Trotsky in 1922. Trotsky later speculated that it may have been due to Kamenev's love of comfort, which Trotsky found "repelled me." He expressed <a class="external text" href="https://www.marxists.org/archive/trotsky/1939/xx/kremlin.htm" rel="nofollow">his feelings to Kamenev</a> in late 1920 or early 1921:<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Our relations with Kamenev, which were very good in the first period after the insurrection, began to become more distant from that day.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-100">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Central Committee's Secretariat became increasingly important during the Civil War and especially in its aftermath, as the Party switched from elected officials to appointed ones. The change was prompted by the need to allocate manpower quickly during the Civil War as well as by the transformation of the party from a small group of revolutionaries into the country's ruling party, with a corresponding increase in membership. New members included career seekers and former members of banned socialist parties, who were viewed with apprehension by Old Bolsheviks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

To prevent a possible degeneration of the party, various membership requirements were instituted for party officials, and the ultimate power of appointment of local officials was reserved for the Secretariat of the Central Committee. This put enormous power in the general secretary's hands.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lenin's <a class="external text" href="https://www.marxists.org/archive/lenin/works/1922/dec/15.htm" rel="nofollow">letter</a> to Stalin dictated on 15 December 1922: "I am sure Trotsky will uphold my views as well as I." Faced with a united opposition by Lenin and Trotsky, the Central Committee reversed its previous decision and adopted the Lenin-Trotsky proposal.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Trotsky explained in Chapter 12 of his unfinished book <a class="external text" href="http://maximumred.blogspot.com/2005_08_01_maximumred_archive.html" rel="nofollow"><i>Stalin</i></a> that he refused to deliver the report because "it seemed to me equivalent to announcing my candidacy for the role of Lenin's successor at a time when Lenin was fighting a grave illness.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Radek wrote:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[101]</a></sup><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r960796168" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The need of the hour was for a man who would incarnate the call to struggle, a man who, subordinating himself completely to the requirements of the struggle, would become the ringing summons to arms, the will which exacts from all unconditional submission to a great, sacrificial necessity. Only a man with Trotsky's capacity for work, only a man so unsparing of himself as Trotsky, only a man who knew how to speak to the soldiers as Trotsky did—only such a man could have become the standard bearer of the armed toilers. He was all things rolled into one.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-115">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The term "Trotskyism" was first coined by the Russian liberal politician Pavel Milyukov, the first foreign minister in the Provisional Government who, in April 1917, was forced to demand that the British government release Trotsky.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-169"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-169">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The murder weapon was an <a href="/wiki/Ice_axe" title="Ice axe">ice axe</a> (and not an <a href="/wiki/Ice_pick" title="Ice pick">ice pick</a> -- an awl-like <a href="/wiki/Bartender" title="Bartender">bartender</a>'s tool); this misnomer has been explained as being occasioned by the assassin's use of the French-language term <i>picolet</i>-- meaning the winter-mountaineering tool which resembles the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pick_axe" title="Pick axe">pick axes</a> used in mining and other excavations, and by the multiple languages spoken by those involved in reporting the details; many history and reference books have confused the two tools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConquest1992418_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConquest1992418-6">[4]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; -webkit-column-width: 25em; column-width: 25em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/Trotsky" rel="nofollow">"Trotsky"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster" title="Merriam-Webster">Merriam-Webster Dictionary</a></i>.</cite><span
